these\n\n1. No backslashes inside f-strings\n2. No nested quotes inside f-strings \u2014 use a variable outside the f-string instead\n3. All POST routing uses elif chains \u2014 never if/elif with a missing first if, never nested if blocks for routing\n4. Never put import statements inside if blocks or functions\n5. All file writes use safe_save_json (tmp file + os.replace) \u2014 never open(f, 'w') directly\n6. No walrus operator (`:=`)\n7. Never use `'\\n'` inside a JS string within a Python string literal \u2014 use `'\\\\n'` so the browser receives the escape sequence, not a raw newline\n8. **multipart/form-data parsing** \u2014 when fetch POSTs use FormData the server receives multipart/form-data not urlencoded. The do_POST handler must sniff Content-Type and parse accordingly using cgi.FieldStorage for multipart. If a POST handler receives empty data check the Content-Type first.\n9. **py_compile passes but runtime fails** \u2014 py_compile only validates syntax not runtime correctness. Always run an in-process smoke test after py_compile to catch NameError, missing variable definitions, and import failures.\n10. **test fixtures must never write to live data** \u2014 verification harnesses must always operate on a temp copy of live data files. Never call save_progress, safe_save_json, or any write helper on live data during testing. Always restore from backup after any test that touches data files.\n11. **double-escaping HTML entities** \u2014 never pass a string that is already HTML-escaped through escape() again. If a string contains literal ampersands for display use plain ampersands in the source string and let escape() handle it once. Strings pre-escaped with `&amp;` will render as visible `&amp;` in the browser if escaped again.\n12. **JS newline in Python f-strings applies everywhere** \u2014 rule 7 applies to ALL files containing JS embedded in Python, not just render_frol_wizard.py. This includes render_schedule.py, render_timeblock.py, render_lucy.py, render_lorenzo.py, and any other render file with inline JavaScript.\n\n### Additional rules (13\u201318)\n\n13. **FROL WIZARD NESTED FORM ADDENDUM** \u2014 The _body_has_form check in _section_chrome looks for `action=\"/frol-wizard\"` in the body string. Any form inside a section body posting to /frol-wizard will suppress the Save and Continue button. Variant tab forms posting to /frol-set-variant are safe. Activity builder forms posting to /frol-add-activity are safe. Before adding any form to a section body confirm its action attribute. This is a recurring bug \u2014 document before fixing if it appears again.\n\n14. **PRE-FLIGHT CHECKLIST** \u2014 Before writing any spec answer these questions. One \u2014 how many files does this touch, list them, if unknown that is a diagnosis step first. Two \u2014 does it involve JavaScript inside Python f-strings, if yes flag the backslash-n rule explicitly in the spec. Three \u2014 does it touch form handling, if yes confirm no nested forms posting to /frol-wizard. Four \u2014 is the root cause confirmed or assumed, if assumed run diagnosis first never draft a fix on an assumed cause. Five \u2014 does it touch multiple files at once, if yes break into separate single-purpose instructions. Six \u2014 does it involve data shape changes or migration, if yes confirm before and after data structure explicitly before writing the spec.\n\n15. **CLAUD.MD READ-BACK REQUIRED** \u2014 At the start of every session read claud.md and paste back every rule found. Then identify which rules apply to today's task. If you cannot paste the rules back accurately stop and ask Lauren to re-paste claud.md before proceeding.\n\n16. **MAGNIFICA HUMANITAS DESIGN PRINCIPLES** \u2014 Every feature built must reflect these principles. One \u2014 the app is a tool not an authority. Every AI suggestion is framed as a suggestion never a prescription. Language uses \"here is one way to think about this\" never \"you should\" or \"the optimal schedule is.\" Two \u2014 companions serve real relationships they do not replace them. Every companion orients toward real people, real community, and real pastoral support. Sister Mary never replaces a confessor. Father Gregory never replaces real mentors. Lucy regularly suggests real conversations over app conversations. Three \u2014 AI supports thinking it does not replace it. Ask before suggesting. Boys build their own plans before seeing AI suggestions. Father Gregory asks questions more than he gives answers. Four \u2014 be transparent about what AI is. Companions never make theological claims with personal authority. Prayer texts come from verified Catholic sources only never AI generated. Five \u2014 language of grace not performance. No gamification no streaks no scores that shame. A hard day is never framed as failure. Sick Day Mode is relief not defeat. Six \u2014 subsidiarity. The family governs itself. Lauren is always the authority. The app serves the family's discernment it does not replace it. Seven \u2014 formation in digital wisdom. Father Gregory teaches the boys to think critically about AI. The explicit goal is that JP finishes high school able to plan his day without the app.\n\n17. **ONE FIX PER INSTRUCTION** \u2014 Never bundle multiple fixes into one Agent instruction unless they are in the same file and directly related. Complex multi-file builds must be broken into sequential single-purpose phases with a compile check and report between each phase.\n\n18. **AUGUST 15TH BUILD PLAN IS THE PRIORITY FILTER** \u2014 Between June 1st and August 15th 2026 every build request must be checked against the August 15th build plan before proceeding. If a requested build is not on the must-have or should-have list for the current week flag it to Lauren before starting. New feature ideas go on the post-September list unless they directly enable one of the 14 goals in the August 15th plan. Scope is the first thing to cut not quality.\n\n### Additional sections of claud.md (not numbered as rules but binding context)\n\n- **What this app is** \u2014 Catholic homeschool family management web app, Python on Replit, single-file HTTP server pattern (app.py + render_*.py), no framework.\n- **Stack** \u2014 Python 3.11; no Flask/Django/FastAPI; JSON files only; plain HTML/CSS/JS rendered as strings; Anthropic via urllib (no SDK).\n- **People** \u2014 Lauren (Mom), John (Dad), JP (14, 9th), Joseph (12, 7th), Michael (5, K), James (13 months, excluded from school/gradebook). Title-case names; Lauren/Mom same person; lowercase keys in auth/pins.json and profiles/.\n- **Data file patterns** \u2014 Most data in data/*.json; person keys title-case in progress/chores/events, lowercase in auth/profiles; progress keys `YYYY-MM-DD::Person::task text`; date keys YYYY-MM-DD (most), YYYY-Www (meal_plan), YYYY-MM (cycle).\n- **Route patterns** \u2014 GET routes call render_*.py functions; POST routes chained as `elif path == \"/route\":` in do_POST; JSON POST bodies must be in `_JSON_PATHS` set or the form-parser eats them.\n- **Anchor-tag navigation** \u2014 Plain `<a href>` can't POST; state must travel in query string OR be persisted before click; destination handler must accept those params AND persist them on arrival. Counter-pattern that bit us: FROL wizard landing anchors `/frol-wizard?step=1&mode=structured`. It does **not** write meal data to `planning_session.json` (it only `advance_planning_session()`s the cursor afterward).\n\n**Is it registered in `_JSON_PATHS`?** **No \u2014 and it doesn't need to be, because it never arrives as a POST body.** `_JSON_PATHS = {\"/plan-import-apply\", \"/plan-import-undo-placement\", \"/curriculum-save\", \"/curriculum-minutes\", \"/poetry-passage-save\"}` (`app.py:3453`). The claud.md `_JSON_PATHS` gotcha only bites routes that send a **raw JSON request body**; neither save channel does.\n\n---\n\n## Report 4 \u2014 Recommended architecture\n\n**The hypothesis is half-right.** The *store* is already unified \u2014 both `[MEAL_UPDATE]` and `/meal-save-plan` persist to the same `data/meal_plan/{Monday}.json` through `save_meal_plan()`. So the bug is **not** \"two competing stores.\" The real architectural mismatch is in the **save trigger and the confirmation loop**:\n\n1. **The trigger is brittle free-text regex.** `_meal_rx` requires a perfectly-formed `[MEAL_UPDATE:Day:slot]\u2026[/MEAL_UPDATE]`. Any LLM malformation \u2014 missing closing tag, stray bracket/whitespace, the `|recipe=` id failing `[^\\s\\[\\]]+` \u2014 silently yields no match \u2192 **no save**, with no signal back to the model.\n2. **Narration is decoupled from persistence.** Lorenzo's \"I saved it / I couldn't save it\" prose is generated by the model *in the same reply, before the server runs the save*. `_save_ok` captures the *real* result but only feeds `_meal_updates_found` / the false-confirmation guard \u2014 it never corrects the words the model already wrote. Hence \"narrates success or failure inconsistently\": the words and the disk state are produced by two different actors and never reconciled.\n3. **Why the card still renders anyway:** when a tag *is* well-formed, the save genuinely succeeds to the authoritative store, so the fridge card updates \u2014 independent of whatever Lorenzo said.\n\n**Minimum change that would make saves reliable** (recommendation only \u2014 not implemented):\n\n- **Keep the unified store** (`save_meal_plan` / `data/meal_plan/{Monday}.json`) \u2014 don't re-route to `planning_session.json`; that's correct as-is.\n- **Make the confirmation server-driven, not model-driven.** After parsing, the server already knows `_save_ok` and `_meal_updates_found`. The smallest reliable fix is to **stop trusting the model's prose for save status**: strip any model-authored save claims and have the server **append a deterministic confirmation/\u25b2failure line** built from `_save_ok` (e.g. \"Saved Monday dinner \u2713\" / \"Couldn't save Monday dinner \u2014 tag was malformed, try again\"). This closes the narration\u2194persistence gap without changing where data lands.\n- **Optionally tighten the channel** by treating the structured `/meal-save-plan` route as the single write path and having the chat handler *call that same save logic* with parsed args (so there's one persistence code path, one place backups/validation live), rather than a second inline `load\u2192mutate\u2192save` copy. This is a refactor, not required for correctness, but it removes the duplicate save spine.\n\nNet: the fix is **confirmation integrity** (server reports the truth of `_save_ok`), not store migration. The `[MEAL_UPDATE]` channel can stay, but its success/failure messaging must be emitted by the server from the actual save result, not narrated by the model.\n\n---\n\nNo files were modified. I'm skipping the code-review step because this task produced **zero code changes** \u2014 it's a read-only diagnosis deliverable, so there's nothing to review. This includes render_schedule.py,\n    60\u2192    render_timeblock.py, render_lucy.py, render_lorenzo.py, and any\n    61\u2192    other render file with inline JavaScript.\n    62\u2192\n    63\u2192## Data file patterns\n    64\u2192- Most data lives in data/*.json as flat dicts or lists\n    65\u2192- Person keys are title-case in progress.json, chores.json, events.json\n    66\u2192- Person keys are lowercase in auth/pins.json and profiles/ (jp.json not JP.json)\n    67\u2192- Progress keys are compound strings: \"YYYY-MM-DD::Person::task text\"\n    68\u2192- Date keys: YYYY-MM-DD (most), YYYY-Www (meal_plan), YYYY-MM (cycle)\n    69\u2192\n    70\u2192## Route patterns\n    71\u2192- GET routes call render_*.py functions that return HTML strings\n    72\u2192- POST routes live in app.py do_POST, chained as elif path == \"/route-name\":\n    73\u2192- JSON POST bodies must be registered in _JSON_PATHS set or the form-parser\n    74\u2192  will consume the payload silently\n    75\u2192- New routes that receive JSON bodies must be added to _JSON_PATHS\n    76\u2192\n    77\u2192## Anchor-tag navigation\n    78\u2192Plain `<a href=\"...\">` links cannot POST and cannot mutate server state on\n    79\u2192their own. Any state the destination page needs must either travel in the\n    80\u2192URL query string OR already be persisted before the user clicks. The\n    81\u2192destination handler is responsible for accepting those query params AND\n    82\u2192persisting them on arrival if they are required for subsequent renders.\n    83\u2192Counter-pattern that bit us: the FROL wizard landing buttons are anchors\n    84\u2192to /frol-wizard?step=1&mode=structured. Without persisting `mode` on the\n    85\u2192first GET, the page's \"is the wizard configured?\" gate kept re-rendering\n    86\u2192the landing screen and the wizard appeared unreachable. If a button must\n    87\u2192trigger persistent state without the destination handler doing the write,\n    88\u2192use a `<form method=\"POST\">` with a submit button styled as a link instead.\n    89\u2192\n    90\u2192## AI calls\n    91\u2192- Model: claude-sonnet-4-20250514\n    92\u2192- Called via urllib.request directly, not the Anthropic SDK\n    93\u2192- API key read from app_settings.json\n    94\u2192- All AI responses go through _repair_and_parse_json() before use\n    95\u2192\n    96\u2192## Change discipline\n    97\u2192- All changes are additive unless explicitly told otherwise\n    98\u2192- Never delete or modify existing behavior unless the task specifically requires it\n    99\u2192- If a task requires editing a file not in the stated scope, stop and flag it\n   100\u2192- Keep modules under 800 lines where possible\n   101\u2192- render_plan_importer.py is 1,114 lines (JS lives in static/js/plan_importer_core.js and static/js/plan_importer_consult.js \u2014 edit those, not the Python file, for JS changes)\n   102\u2192\n   103\u2192## FROL Wizard form bypass trap\n   104\u2192The _section_chrome function in render_frol_wizard.py suppresses the\n   105\u2192Save and Continue button when it detects a form in the body via the\n   106\u2192_body_has_form check. This check currently looks for action=\"/frol-wizard\"\n   107\u2192in the body. Any utility form in a section body that posts to\n   108\u2192/frol-wizard will incorrectly suppress the Save and Continue button.\n   109\u2192Utility forms that post to other routes (like /frol-set-variant,\n   110\u2192/frol-add-activity, /frol-delete-activity) are safe and will not trigger\n   111\u2192the bypass. When adding new forms to section bodies always check whether\n   112\u2192they post to /frol-wizard and if so either use a different route or\n   113\u2192handle the advance separately in the section body itself.\n   114\u2192\n   115\u2192## Additional rules (13\u201319)\n   116\u2192\n   117\u219213. **FROL WIZARD NESTED FORM ADDENDUM** \u2014 The _body_has_form check in\n   118\u2192    _section_chrome looks for action=\u201d/frol-wizard\u201d in the body string.\n   119\u2192    Any form inside a section body posting to /frol-wizard will suppress\n   120\u2192    the Save and Continue button. Variant tab forms posting to\n   121\u2192    /frol-set-variant are safe. Activity builder forms posting to\n   122\u2192    /frol-add-activity are safe. Before adding any form to a section body\n   123\u2192    confirm its action attribute. This is a recurring bug \u2014 document\n   124\u2192    before fixing if it appears again.\n   125\u2192\n   126\u219214. **PRE-FLIGHT CHECKLIST** \u2014 Before writing any spec answer these\n   127\u2192    questions. One \u2014 how many files does this touch, list them, if\n   128\u2192    unknown that is a diagnosis step first. Two \u2014 does it involve\n   129\u2192    JavaScript inside Python f-strings, if yes flag the backslash-n rule\n   130\u2192    explicitly in the spec. Three \u2014 does it touch form handling, if yes\n   131\u2192    confirm no nested forms posting to /frol-wizard. Four \u2014 is the root\n   132\u2192    cause confirmed or assumed, if assumed run diagnosis first never\n   133\u2192    draft a fix on an assumed cause. Five \u2014 does it touch multiple files\n   134\u2192    at once, if yes break into separate single-purpose instructions.\n   135\u2192    Six \u2014 does it involve data shape changes or migration, if yes\n   136\u2192    confirm before and after data structure explicitly before writing\n   137\u2192    the spec.\n   138\u2192\n   139\u219215. **CLAUD.MD READ-BACK REQUIRED** \u2014 At the start of every session read\n   140\u2192    claud.md and paste back every rule found. One \u2014 the app is a tool not an authority.\n   146\u2192    Every AI suggestion is framed as a suggestion never a prescription.\n   147\u2192    Language uses \u201chere is one way to think about this\u201d never \u201cyou\n   148\u2192    should\u201d or \u201cthe optimal schedule is.\u201d Two \u2014 companions serve real\n   149\u2192    relationships they do not replace them. ./attached_assets/Pasted-Build-the-curriculum-to-POD-bridge-Plan-before-building_1777720622839.txt:Build the curriculum-to-POD bridge. Plan before building. Edit only daily_schedule_engine.py, data_helpers.py, and app.py. No other files. What and why: curriculum.json contains JP and Joseph’s full 32-week lesson sequence but is currently disconnected from their POD. school_weeks.json drives the POD today but only holds one week at a time from a PDF upload. This build re-enables the curriculum merge so the full sequence drives the POD, adds the frequency filter so subjects only appear on their meeting days, and wires auto-advance so completing a lesson moves the cursor forward automatically. Change 1 — data_helpers.py: Add three new helper functions. First, subject_meeting_days(child, subject) reads data/school_weeks.json via load_school_weeks(), inverts the parsed_days structure to find which weekday names the subject appears on for that child, and returns a list of weekday name strings like [“Monday”, “Wednesday”, “Friday”]. Returns an empty list if the subject is not found. Second, subject_day_index(meeting_days, today_name) takes a list of weekday names and today’s weekday name, sorts the meeting_days list using WEEKDAY_ORDER from config.py for stable ordering, and returns the 1-based position of today_name within the sorted list, or None if today_name is not in the list. Third, advance_curriculum_cursor(child, subject) loads curriculum.json, finds the subject node for that child, reads _current_week and _current_day, gets the current week’s segments via week_day_segments, increments _current_day to the next segment index, and when _current_day exceeds the last segment rolls over to _current_week + 1 and resets _current_day to the first segment index of the new week. When _current_week exceeds the total number of week keys on the subject node mark the subject complete by setting _current_week to 999 and _current_day to 1, then append a note to notes.json using the existing note append pattern with text saying the child has completed the subject and all weeks are done with suggested_destination set to /curriculum. Save curriculum.json with save_curriculum. Wrap everything in try/except so a failure never crashes the caller. Change 2 — daily_schedule_engine.py: Replace the commented-out curriculum merge block at lines 429-454 with a modernized version. The new block should import load_curriculum, get_curriculum_week, resolve_week_text, week_day_segments, subject_meeting_days, subject_day_index from data_helpers. For each subject in the child’s curriculum skipping subjects where _current_week >= 999, call subject_meeting_days(child, subject) to get the subject’s meeting days. Call subject_day_index(meeting_days, weekday) where weekday is the current day name passed into extract_school_tasks_for_child. If subject_day_index returns None the subject does not meet today — skip it. If the subject is already in seen_subjects skip it. Otherwise call resolve_week_text(subject_node, subj_week, day_pref=day_index) to get today’s assignment text. If text is non-empty build a task dict. For math detection use “algebra” in subject.lower() or “math” in subject.lower(). Use the same math checklist pattern as the live PDF path including _get_brother_math_label for the brother cross-check items. Add from_curriculum=True to the task dict. Wrap the entire block in try/except pass. Change 3 — app.py: In the /toggle-task handler after the set_task_done call, add a curriculum advance block. When _done is True and the task ID contains SCHOOL either as ::SCHOOL:: or starts with SCHOOL:: extract the subject name by splitting on :: and taking the element immediately after SCHOOL. Only advance when the checklist item contains “Assignment completed”. Extract the child name from the task ID using the same split logic. Call advance_curriculum_cursor(child, subject) from data_helpers. Wrap in try/except. Verify: run py_compile on all three files. Confirm subject_meeting_days returns the correct days for JP/Music 8. Confirm subject_day_index returns 1 for Wednesday/Wednesday and None for Wednesday/Monday. Confirm the commented-out block is fully replaced not just uncommented. Plan before building.

./attached_assets/Pasted-Read-claud-md-first-Two-tasks-Task-1-add-five-new-rules_1779278815327.txt:Read claud.md first. Two tasks. Task 1 — add five new rules to claud.md. Rule 1 — multipart/form-data parsing: when fetch POSTs use FormData the server receives multipart/form-data not urlencoded. The do_POST handler must sniff Content-Type and parse accordingly using cgi.FieldStorage for multipart. If a POST handler receives empty data check the Content-Type first. Rule 2 — py_compile passes but runtime fails: py_compile only validates syntax not runtime correctness. Always run an in-process smoke test after py_compile to catch NameError, missing variable definitions, and import failures. Rule 3 — test fixtures must never write to live data: verification harnesses must always operate on a temp copy of live data files. Never call save_progress, safe_save_json, or any write helper on live data during testing. Always restore from backup after any test that touches data files. Rule 4 — double-escaping HTML entities: never pass a string that is already HTML-escaped through escape() again. If a string contains literal ampersands for display use plain ampersands in the source string and let escape() handle it once. Strings pre-escaped with & will render as visible & in the browser if escaped again. Rule 5 — JS newline in Python f-strings applies everywhere: claud.md rule 7 (never use backslash-n in JS strings inside Python f-strings) applies to ALL files containing JS embedded in Python, not just render_frol_wizard.py. This includes render_schedule.py, render_timeblock.py, render_lucy.py, render_lorenzo.py, and any other render file with inline JavaScript. Task 2 — fix the Section 12 Save and Continue button not working. In render_frol_wizard.py find where _section_chrome renders the advance button for section 12. Check whether frolAdvance in static/js/frol_wizard.js is correctly intercepting the form submit for section 12 — specifically check if the data-step attribute on the form matches what frolAdvance expects and whether the advance_v2 POST handler in app.py has a branch for section 12. Paste the relevant code and fix any mismatch. Run py_compile after. No other changes.

Parser spine, verbatim (`app.py:5806\u20135907`):\n\n```python\n                # \u2500\u2500 Parse [MEAL_UPDATE:Day:slot[|recipe=ID]]meal[/MEAL_UPDATE] and save \u2500\u2500\n                _meal_rx = _re.compile(\n                    r'\\[MEAL_UPDATE:([^:\\]]+):([^|\\]]+)(?:\\|recipe=([^\\]]+))?\\]'\n                    r'([\\s\\S]*?)\\[\\/MEAL_UPDATE\\]',\n                    _re.IGNORECASE\n                )\n                try:\n                    from render_meals import MEAL_SLOT_SET as _DICT_OK_SLOTS\n                except Exception:\n                    _DICT_OK_SLOTS = {\"breakfast\",\"lunch\",\"dinner\",\"dessert\",\"snacks\",\"dad_lunch\"}\n                _meal_updates_found = []\n                for _mm in _meal_rx.finditer(text):\n                    _mday  = _mm.group(1).strip()\n                    _mslot = _mm.group(2).strip().lower()\n                    _mrid  = (_mm.group(3) or \"\").strip()\n                    if _mrid and not _re.fullmatch(r\"[^\\s\\[\\]]+\", _mrid):\n                        print(f\"[lorenzo MEAL_UPDATE] rejected malformed recipe_id: {_mrid!r}\")\n                        _mrid = \"\"\n                    _mmeal = _mm.group(4).strip()\n                    if _mday and _mslot:\n                        _save_ok = False\n                        try:\n                            _wk = _planning_week_key()\n                            _plan = load_meal_plan(_wk)\n                            if _mmeal:\n                                if _mrid and _mslot in _DICT_OK_SLOTS:\n                                    _plan[\"days\"].setdefault(_mday, {})[_mslot] = {\n                                        \"display\":   _mmeal,\n                                        \"recipe_id\": _mrid,\n                                    }\n                                    # [enrichment block elided for length \u2014 app.py:5847\u20135894:\n                                    #  for recipe-linked dinners, fills prep_time/cook_time from\n                                    #  the recipe card, kid 'helpers' via kid_helpers.assign_kid_steps,\n                                    #  and serve_time from the FROL; \"fill blanks only\".]\n                                else:\n                                    _plan[\"days\"].setdefault(_mday, {})[_mslot] = _mmeal\n                            else:\n                                _plan[\"days\"].setdefault(_mday, {}).pop(_mslot, None)\n                            _plan[\"start\"] = _plan.get(\"start\") or _wk\n                            save_meal_plan(_plan)\n                            _save_ok = True\n                        except Exception as _se:\n                            print(f\"[lorenzo MEAL_UPDATE] save failed for {_mday}/{_mslot}: {_se}\")\n                        if _save_ok:\n                            _meal_updates_found.append((_mday, _mslot))\n```\n\n**Where does it write?** To the **`/meal-save-plan` store** \u2014 i.e. the same `data/meal_plan/{Monday}.json`, via the same `save_meal_plan()`. It does **not** write meal data to `planning_session.json` (it only `advance_planning_session()`s the cursor afterward).\n\n**Is it registered in `_JSON_PATHS`?** **No \u2014 and it doesn't need to be, because it never arrives as a POST body.** `_JSON_PATHS = {\"/plan-import-apply\", \"/plan-import-undo-placement\", \"/curriculum-save\", \"/curriculum-minutes\", \"/poetry-passage-save\"}` (`app.py:3453`). The claud.md `_JSON_PATHS` gotcha only bites routes that send a **raw JSON request body**; neither save channel does.\n\n---\n\n## Report 4 \u2014 Recommended architecture\n\n**The hypothesis is half-right.** The *store* is already unified \u2014 both `[MEAL_UPDATE]` and `/meal-save-plan` persist to the same `data/meal_plan/{Monday}.json` through `save_meal_plan()`. So the bug is **not** \"two competing stores.\" The real architectural mismatch is in the **save trigger and the confirmation loop**:\n\n1. **The trigger is brittle free-text regex.** `_meal_rx` requires a perfectly-formed `[MEAL_UPDATE:Day:slot]\u2026[/MEAL_UPDATE]`. Any LLM malformation \u2014 missing closing tag, stray bracket/whitespace, the `|recipe=` id failing `[^\\s\\[\\]]+` \u2014 silently yields no match \u2192 **no save**, with no signal back to the model.\n2. **Narration is decoupled from persistence.** Lorenzo's \"I saved it / I couldn't save it\" prose is generated by the model *in the same reply, before the server runs the save*. `_save_ok` captures the *real* result but only feeds `_meal_updates_found` / the false-confirmation guard \u2014 it never corrects the words the model already wrote. Hence \"narrates success or failure inconsistently\": the words and the disk state are produced by two different actors and never reconciled.\n3. **Why the card still renders anyway:** when a tag *is* well-formed, the save genuinely succeeds to the authoritative store, so the fridge card updates \u2014 independent of whatever Lorenzo said.\n\n**Minimum change that would make saves reliable** (recommendation only \u2014 not implemented):\n\n- **Keep the unified store** (`save_meal_plan` / `data/meal_plan/{Monday}.json`) \u2014 don't re-route to `planning_session.json`; that's correct as-is.\n- **Make the confirmation server-driven, not model-driven.** After parsing, the server already knows `_save_ok` and `_meal_updates_found`. The smallest reliable fix is to **stop trusting the model's prose for save status**: strip any model-authored save claims and have the server **append a deterministic confirmation/\u25b2failure line** built from `_save_ok` (e.g. \"Saved Monday dinner \u2713\" / \"Couldn't save Monday dinner \u2014 tag was malformed, try again\"). This closes the narration\u2194persistence gap without changing where data lands.\n- **Optionally tighten the channel** by treating the structured `/meal-save-plan` route as the single write path and having the chat handler *call that same save logic* with parsed args (so there's one persistence code path, one place backups/validation live), rather than a second inline `load\u2192mutate\u2192save` copy. This is a refactor, not required for correctness, but it removes the duplicate save spine.\n\nNet: the fix is **confirmation integrity** (server reports the truth of `_save_ok`), not store migration. The `[MEAL_UPDATE]` channel can stay, but its success/failure messaging must be emitted by the server from the actual save result, not narrated by the model.\n\n---\n\nNo files were modified. Parser spine, verbatim (`app.py:5806\u20135907`):\n\n```python\n                # \u2500\u2500 Parse [MEAL_UPDATE:Day:slot[|recipe=ID]]meal[/MEAL_UPDATE] and save \u2500\u2500\n                _meal_rx = _re.compile(\n                    r'\\[MEAL_UPDATE:([^:\\]]+):([^|\\]]+)(?:\\|recipe=([^\\]]+))?\\]'\n                    r'([\\s\\S]*?)\\[\\/MEAL_UPDATE\\]',\n                    _re.IGNORECASE\n                )\n                try:\n                    from render_meals import MEAL_SLOT_SET as _DICT_OK_SLOTS\n                except Exception:\n                    _DICT_OK_SLOTS = {\"breakfast\",\"lunch\",\"dinner\",\"dessert\",\"snacks\",\"dad_lunch\"}\n                _meal_updates_found = []\n                for _mm in _meal_rx.finditer(text):\n                    _mday  = _mm.group(1).strip()\n                    _mslot = _mm.group(2).strip().lower()\n                    _mrid  = (_mm.group(3) or \"\").strip()\n                    if _mrid and not _re.fullmatch(r\"[^\\s\\[\\]]+\", _mrid):\n                        print(f\"[lorenzo MEAL_UPDATE] rejected malformed recipe_id: {_mrid!r}\")\n                        _mrid = \"\"\n                    _mmeal = _mm.group(4).strip()\n                    if _mday and _mslot:\n                        _save_ok = False\n                        try:\n                            _wk = _planning_week_key()\n                            _plan = load_meal_plan(_wk)\n                            if _mmeal:\n                                if _mrid and _mslot in _DICT_OK_SLOTS:\n                                    _plan[\"days\"].setdefault(_mday, {})[_mslot] = {\n                                        \"display\":   _mmeal,\n                                        \"recipe_id\": _mrid,\n                                    }\n                                    # [enrichment block elided for length \u2014 app.py:5847\u20135894:\n                                    #  for recipe-linked dinners, fills prep_time/cook_time from\n                                    #  the recipe card, kid 'helpers' via kid_helpers.assign_kid_steps,\n                                    #  and serve_time from the FROL; \"fill blanks only\".]\n                                else:\n                                    _plan[\"days\"].setdefault(_mday, {})[_mslot] = _mmeal\n                            else:\n                                _plan[\"days\"].setdefault(_mday, {}).pop(_mslot, None)\n                            _plan[\"start\"] = _plan.get(\"start\") or _wk\n                            save_meal_plan(_plan)\n                            _save_ok = True\n                        except Exception as _se:\n                            print(f\"[lorenzo MEAL_UPDATE] save failed for {_mday}/{_mslot}: {_se}\")\n                        if _save_ok:\n                            _meal_updates_found.append((_mday, _mslot))\n```\n\n**Where does it write?** To the **`/meal-save-plan` store** \u2014 i.e. the same `data/meal_plan/{Monday}.json`, via the same `save_meal_plan()`. It does **not** write meal data to `planning_session.json` (it only `advance_planning_session()`s the cursor afterward).\n\n**Is it registered in `_JSON_PATHS`?** **No \u2014 and it doesn't need to be, because it never arrives as a POST body.** `_JSON_PATHS = {\"/plan-import-apply\", \"/plan-import-undo-placement\", \"/curriculum-save\", \"/curriculum-minutes\", \"/poetry-passage-save\"}` (`app.py:3453`). The `[MEAL_UPDATE]` text is extracted from the *LLM response*, not from the request body, so the form-parser-consumes-JSON trap (claud.md) cannot apply to it. \n\nWorth noting for completeness: **`/meal-save-plan` is also not in `_JSON_PATHS`, and that is correct** \u2014 it posts `application/x-www-form-urlencoded` fields (`week=\u2026`, `days=<JSON string>`) and `json.loads` the `days` field itself, so the urlencoded parser handles it fine. The claud.md `_JSON_PATHS` gotcha only bites routes that send a **raw JSON request body**; neither save channel does.\n\n---\n\n## Report 4 \u2014 Recommended architecture\n\n**The hypothesis is half-right.** The *store* is already unified \u2014 both `[MEAL_UPDATE]` and `/meal-save-plan` persist to the same `data/meal_plan/{Monday}.json` through `save_meal_plan()`. So the bug is **not** \"two competing stores.\" The real architectural mismatch is in the **save trigger and the confirmation loop**:\n\n1. **The trigger is brittle free-text regex.** `_meal_rx` requires a perfectly-formed `[MEAL_UPDATE:Day:slot]\u2026[/MEAL_UPDATE]`. Any LLM malformation \u2014 missing closing tag, stray bracket/whitespace, the `|recipe=` id failing `[^\\s\\[\\]]+` \u2014 silently yields no match \u2192 **no save**, with no signal back to the model.\n2. **Narration is decoupled from persistence.** Lorenzo's \"I saved it / I couldn't save it\" prose is generated by the model *in the same reply, before the server runs the save*. `_save_ok` captures the *real* result but only feeds `_meal_updates_found` / the false-confirmation guard \u2014 it never corrects the words the model already wrote. Hence \"narrates success or failure inconsistently\": the words and the disk state are produced by two different actors and never reconciled.\n3. **Why the card still renders anyway:** when a tag *is* well-formed, the save genuinely succeeds to the authoritative store, so the fridge card updates \u2014 independent of whatever Lorenzo said.\n\n**Minimum change that would make saves reliable** (recommendation only \u2014 not implemented):\n\n- **Keep the unified store** (`save_meal_plan` / `data/meal_plan/{Monday}.json`) \u2014 don't re-route to `planning_session.json`; that's correct as-is.\n- **Make the confirmation server-driven, not model-driven.** After parsing, the server already knows `_save_ok` and `_meal_updates_found`. The smallest reliable fix is to **stop trusting the model's prose for save status**: strip any model-authored save claims and have the server **append a deterministic confirmation/\u25b2failure line** built from `_save_ok` (e.g. \"Saved Monday dinner \u2713\" / \"Couldn't save Monday dinner \u2014 tag was malformed, try again\"). This closes the narration\u2194persistence gap without changing where data lands.\n- **Optionally tighten the channel** by treating the structured `/meal-save-plan` route as the single write path and having the chat handler *call that same save logic* with parsed args (so there's one persistence code path, one place backups/validation live), rather than a second inline `load\u2192mutate\u2192save` copy. This is a refactor, not required for correctness, but it removes the duplicate save spine.\n\nNet: the fix is **confirmation integrity** (server reports the truth of `_save_ok`), not store migration. The `[MEAL_UPDATE]` channel can stay, but its success/failure messaging must be emitted by the server from the actual save result, not narrated by the model.\n\n---\n\nNo files were modified. Parser spine, verbatim (`app.py:5806\u20135907`):\n\n```python\n                # \u2500\u2500 Parse [MEAL_UPDATE:Day:slot[|recipe=ID]]meal[/MEAL_UPDATE] and save \u2500\u2500\n                _meal_rx = _re.compile(\n                    r'\\[MEAL_UPDATE:([^:\\]]+):([^|\\]]+)(?:\\|recipe=([^\\]]+))?\\]'\n                    r'([\\s\\S]*?)\\[\\/MEAL_UPDATE\\]',\n                    _re.IGNORECASE\n                )\n                try:\n                    from render_meals import MEAL_SLOT_SET as _DICT_OK_SLOTS\n                except Exception:\n                    _DICT_OK_SLOTS = {\"breakfast\",\"lunch\",\"dinner\",\"dessert\",\"snacks\",\"dad_lunch\"}\n                _meal_updates_found = []\n                for _mm in _meal_rx.finditer(text):\n                    _mday  = _mm.group(1).strip()\n                    _mslot = _mm.group(2).strip().lower()\n                    _mrid  = (_mm.group(3) or \"\").strip()\n                    if _mrid and not _re.fullmatch(r\"[^\\s\\[\\]]+\", _mrid):\n                        print(f\"[lorenzo MEAL_UPDATE] rejected malformed recipe_id: {_mrid!r}\")\n                        _mrid = \"\"\n                    _mmeal = _mm.group(4).strip()\n                    if _mday and _mslot:\n                        _save_ok = False\n                        try:\n                            _wk = _planning_week_key()\n                            _plan = load_meal_plan(_wk)\n                            if _mmeal:\n                                if _mrid and _mslot in _DICT_OK_SLOTS:\n                                    _plan[\"days\"].setdefault(_mday, {})[_mslot] = {\n                                        \"display\":   _mmeal,\n                                        \"recipe_id\": _mrid,\n                                    }\n                                    # [enrichment block elided for length \u2014 app.py:5847\u20135894:\n                                    #  for recipe-linked dinners, fills prep_time/cook_time from\n                                    #  the recipe card, kid 'helpers' via kid_helpers.assign_kid_steps,\n                                    #  and serve_time from the FROL; \"fill blanks only\".]\n                                else:\n                                    _plan[\"days\"].setdefault(_mday, {})[_mslot] = _mmeal\n                            else:\n                                _plan[\"days\"].setdefault(_mday, {}).pop(_mslot, None)\n                            _plan[\"start\"] = _plan.get(\"start\") or _wk\n                            save_meal_plan(_plan)\n                            _save_ok = True\n                        except Exception as _se:\n                            print(f\"[lorenzo MEAL_UPDATE] save failed for {_mday}/{_mslot}: {_se}\")\n                        if _save_ok:\n                            _meal_updates_found.append((_mday, _mslot))\n```\n\n**Where does it write?** To the **`/meal-save-plan` store** \u2014 i.e. the same `data/meal_plan/{Monday}.json`, via the same `save_meal_plan()`. It does **not** write meal data to `planning_session.json` (it only `advance_planning_session()`s the cursor afterward).\n\n**Is it registered in `_JSON_PATHS`?** **No \u2014 and it doesn't need to be, because it never arrives as a POST body.** `_JSON_PATHS = {\"/plan-import-apply\", \"/plan-import-undo-placement\", \"/curriculum-save\", \"/curriculum-minutes\", \"/poetry-passage-save\"}` (`app.py:3453`). The `[MEAL_UPDATE]` text is extracted from the *LLM response*, not from the request body, so the form-parser-consumes-JSON trap (claud.md) cannot apply to it. \n\nWorth noting for completeness: **`/meal-save-plan` is also not in `_JSON_PATHS`, and that is correct** \u2014 it posts `application/x-www-form-urlencoded` fields (`week=\u2026`, `days=<JSON string>`) and `json.loads` the `days` field itself, so the urlencoded parser handles it fine. The claud.md `_JSON_PATHS` gotcha only bites routes that send a **raw JSON request body**; neither save channel does.\n\n---\n\n## Report 4 \u2014 Recommended architecture\n\n**The hypothesis is half-right.** The *store* is already unified \u2014 both `[MEAL_UPDATE]` and `/meal-save-plan` persist to the same `data/meal_plan/{Monday}.json` through `save_meal_plan()`. So the bug is **not** \"two competing stores.\" The real architectural mismatch is in the **save trigger and the confirmation loop**:\n\n1. **The trigger is brittle free-text regex.** `_meal_rx` requires a perfectly-formed `[MEAL_UPDATE:Day:slot]\u2026[/MEAL_UPDATE]`. Any LLM malformation \u2014 missing closing tag, stray bracket/whitespace, the `|recipe=` id failing `[^\\s\\[\\]]+` \u2014 silently yields no match \u2192 **no save**, with no signal back to the model.\n2. **Narration is decoupled from persistence.** Lorenzo's \"I saved it / I couldn't save it\" prose is generated by the model *in the same reply, before the server runs the save*. `_save_ok` captures the *real* result but only feeds `_meal_updates_found` / the false-confirmation guard \u2014 it never corrects the words the model already wrote. Hence \"narrates success or failure inconsistently\": the words and the disk state are produced by two different actors and never reconciled.\n3. **Why the card still renders anyway:** when a tag *is* well-formed, the save genuinely succeeds to the authoritative store, so the fridge card updates \u2014 independent of whatever Lorenzo said.\n\n**Minimum change that would make saves reliable** (recommendation only \u2014 not implemented):\n\n- **Keep the unified store** (`save_meal_plan` / `data/meal_plan/{Monday}.json`) \u2014 don't re-route to `planning_session.json`; that's correct as-is.\n- **Make the confirmation server-driven, not model-driven.** After parsing, the server already knows `_save_ok` and `_meal_updates_found`. The smallest reliable fix is to **stop trusting the model's prose for save status**: strip any model-authored save claims and have the server **append a deterministic confirmation/\u25b2failure line** built from `_save_ok` (e.g. \"Saved Monday dinner \u2713\" / \"Couldn't save Monday dinner \u2014 tag was malformed, try again\"). This closes the narration\u2194persistence gap without changing where data lands.\n- **Optionally tighten the channel** by treating the structured `/meal-save-plan` route as the single write path and having the chat handler *call that same save logic* with parsed args (so there's one persistence code path, one place backups/validation live), rather than a second inline `load\u2192mutate\u2192save` copy. This is a refactor, not required for correctness, but it removes the duplicate save spine.\n\nNet: the fix is **confirmation integrity** (server reports the truth of `_save_ok`), not store migration. The `[MEAL_UPDATE]` channel can stay, but its success/failure messaging must be emitted by the server from the actual save result, not narrated by the model.\n\n---\n\nNo files were modified.
